For the former autonomous state in southern Arabia, see <a href="/wiki/Qu%27aiti" title="Qu&#39;aiti">Qu'aiti</a>. For the city, see <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_City" title="Kuwait City">Kuwait City</a>.</div>

</ol></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Kuwait</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/ʊ/: &#39;u&#39; in &#39;push&#39;">ʊ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;w&#39; in &#39;wind&#39;">w</span><span title="/eɪ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;face&#39;">eɪ</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span></span>/</a></span>&#32;<span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Kuwait.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/64/En-us-Kuwait.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Kuwait.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">الكويت</span>&#8206; <i><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">al-Kuwait</i></i>, <small>Gulf Arabic pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Arabic" title="Help:IPA/Arabic">[ɪl‿ɪkweːt]</a></span> or <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Arabic" title="Help:IPA/Arabic">[lɪkweːt]</a></span>), officially the <b>State of Kuwait</b> (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">دولة الكويت</span>&#8206; <i><span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ar-State_of_Kuwait.oga" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/69/Ar-State_of_Kuwait.oga" class="internal" title="Ar-State of Kuwait.oga">Dawlat al-Kuwait</a></span></span></i>), is a country in <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a>. Situated in the northern edge of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Arabia" title="Eastern Arabia">Eastern Arabia</a> at the tip of the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a>, it shares borders with <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>. As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Kuwait has a population of 4.5&#160;million people: 1.3 million are Kuwaitis and 3.2 million are expatriates.<sup id="cite_ref-census_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Expatriates_in_Kuwait" title="Expatriates in Kuwait">Expatriates</a> account for 70% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Oil_reserves" title="Oil reserves">Oil reserves</a> were discovered in commercial quantities in 1938. From 1946 to 1982, the country underwent large-scale modernization. In the 1980s, Kuwait experienced a period of geopolitical instability and an economic crisis following the <a href="/wiki/Souk_Al-Manakh_stock_market_crash" title="Souk Al-Manakh stock market crash">stock market crash</a>. In 1990, Kuwait was <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Kuwait" title="Invasion of Kuwait">invaded</a>, and later <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Governorate" title="Kuwait Governorate">annexed</a>, by <a href="/wiki/Ba%27athist_Iraq" title="Ba&#39;athist Iraq">Saddam's Iraq</a>. The Iraqi occupation of Kuwait came to an end in 1991 after <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">military intervention</a> by a military coalition led by the United States. Kuwait is a <a href="/wiki/Major_non-NATO_ally" title="Major non-NATO ally">major non-NATO ally</a> of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> It is also a major ally of <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations" title="Association of Southeast Asian Nations">ASEAN</a>, while maintaining a strong relationship with <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto1_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto2_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kuwait is a constitutional <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Semi-democracy" title="Semi-democracy">semi-democratic</a> political system. Kuwait has a <a href="/wiki/High-income_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="High-income economy">high-income economy</a> backed by the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_proven_oil_reserves#Countries" title="List of countries by proven oil reserves">sixth largest oil reserves</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Kuwaiti_dinar" title="Kuwaiti dinar">Kuwaiti dinar</a> is the highest valued currency in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-curr_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-curr-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, the country has the fourth <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita#List_of_countries_and_dependencies" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">highest per capita income</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Kuwait" title="Constitution of Kuwait">Constitution</a> was <a href="/wiki/Promulgated" class="mw-redirect" title="Promulgated">promulgated</a> in 1962.<sup id="cite_ref-ras_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ras-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rsf_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rsf-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wsjo_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsjo-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait is home to the largest <a href="/wiki/Sheikh_Jaber_Al-Ahmad_Cultural_Centre" title="Sheikh Jaber Al-Ahmad Cultural Centre">opera house</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_National_Cultural_District" title="Kuwait National Cultural District">Kuwait National Cultural District</a> is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Global_Cultural_Districts_Network" title="Global Cultural Districts Network">Global Cultural Districts Network</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gcdn_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gcdn-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Kuwait" title="History of Kuwait">History of Kuwait</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1613, the town of Kuwait was founded in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_City" title="Kuwait City">Kuwait City</a>. Administratively, it was a sheikhdom, ruled by local <a href="/wiki/Sheikhs" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheikhs">sheikhs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Farah_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Farah-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-casey_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-casey-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In 1716, the <a href="/wiki/Bani_Utub" class="mw-redirect" title="Bani Utub">Bani Utub</a> settled in Kuwait, which at this time was inhabited by a few <a href="/wiki/Fishermen" class="mw-redirect" title="Fishermen">fishermen</a> and primarily functioned as a <a href="/wiki/Fishing_village" title="Fishing village">fishing village</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> In the eighteenth century, Kuwait prospered and rapidly became the principal commercial center for the transit of goods between <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muscat,_Oman" class="mw-redirect" title="Muscat, Oman">Muscat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arabia" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabia">Arabia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sail_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sail-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> By the mid 1700s, Kuwait had already established itself as the major trading route from the Persian Gulf to <a href="/wiki/Aleppo" title="Aleppo">Aleppo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kw_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kw-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman%E2%80%93Persian_War_(1775%E2%80%9376)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman–Persian War (1775–76)">Persian siege of Basra in 1775–79</a>, Iraqi merchants took refuge in Kuwait and were partly instrumental in the expansion of Kuwait's boat-building and trading activities.<sup id="cite_ref-boom_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boom-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> As a result, Kuwait's maritime commerce boomed,<sup id="cite_ref-boom_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boom-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> as the Indian trade routes with Baghdad, Aleppo, <a href="/wiki/Smyrna" title="Smyrna">Smyrna</a> and <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> were diverted to Kuwait during this time.<sup id="cite_ref-kw_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kw-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a> was diverted to Kuwait in 1792.<sup id="cite_ref-eas_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eas-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The East India Company secured the sea routes between Kuwait, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> and the east coasts of <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-eas_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eas-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> After the Persians withdrew from <a href="/wiki/Basra" title="Basra">Basra</a> in 1779, Kuwait continued to attract trade away from Basra.<sup id="cite_ref-mer_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mer-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kuwait was the center of <a href="/wiki/Boat_building" title="Boat building">boat building</a> in the Persian Gulf region.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> During the late eighteenth and nineteenth centuries, vessels made in Kuwait carried the bulk of trade between the ports of India, East Africa and the Red Sea.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Kuwaiti ships were renowned throughout the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a>. Regional geopolitical turbulence helped foster <a href="/wiki/Prosperity" title="Prosperity">economic prosperity</a> in Kuwait in the second half of the 18th century.<sup id="cite_ref-jasser_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jasser-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Perhaps the biggest catalyst for much of Kuwait becoming prosperous was due to Basra's instability in the late 18th century.<sup id="cite_ref-w_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> In the late 18th century, Kuwait partly functioned as a haven for Basra's merchants, who were fleeing <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman government">Ottoman government</a> persecution.<sup id="cite_ref-halamudhir_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-halamudhir-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Kuwaitis developed a reputation as the best sailors in the Persian Gulf.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="British_Protectorate_.281899-1961.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="British_Protectorate_(1899-1961)">British Protectorate (1899-1961)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: British Protectorate (1899-1961)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the 1890s, Kuwait was threatened by the Ottoman Empire. In a bid to address its security issues, the then ruler, Sheikh <a href="/wiki/Mubarak_Al-Sabah" title="Mubarak Al-Sabah">Mubarak Al Sabah</a> signed an agreement with the <a href="/wiki/British_India" class="mw-redirect" title="British India">British government in India</a>, subsequently known as the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Kuwaiti_Agreement_of_1899" title="Anglo-Kuwaiti Agreement of 1899">Anglo-Kuwaiti Agreement of 1899</a> and became a <a href="/wiki/British_protectorate" title="British protectorate">British protectorate</a>. This gave Britain exclusivity of access and trade with Kuwait, and excluded Iraq to the north from a port on the Persian Gulf. The Sheikhdom of Kuwait remained a British protectorate from 1899 (until 1961).<sup id="cite_ref-Farah_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Farah-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-casey_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-casey-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kuwait1944.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Kuwait1944.jpg/250px-Kuwait1944.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="207" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Kuwait1944.jpg/375px-Kuwait1944.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Kuwait1944.jpg/500px-Kuwait1944.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="497" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kuwait1944.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Celebration at <a href="/wiki/Seif_Palace" title="Seif Palace">Seif Palace</a> in 1944</div></div></div>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Kuwait%E2%80%93Najd_War" title="Kuwait–Najd War">Kuwait–Najd War</a> of 1919–20, <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Saud" title="Ibn Saud">Ibn Saud</a> imposed a trade blockade against Kuwait from the years 1923 until 1937.<sup id="cite_ref-do_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-do-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The goal of the Saudi economic and military attacks on Kuwait was to annex as much of Kuwait's territory as possible. At the <a href="/wiki/Uqair_Protocol_of_1922" title="Uqair Protocol of 1922">Uqair conference</a> in 1922, the boundaries of Kuwait and <a href="/wiki/Najd" title="Najd">Najd</a> were set; as a result of British interference, Kuwait had no representative at the <a href="/wiki/Uqair_Protocol_of_1922" title="Uqair Protocol of 1922">Uqair conference</a>. Ibn Saud persuaded <a href="/wiki/Percy_Cox" title="Percy Cox">Sir Percy Cox</a> to give him two-thirds of Kuwait's territory. More than half of Kuwait was lost due to Uqair. After the Uqair conference, Kuwait was still subjected to a Saudi economic blockade and intermittent Saudi <a href="/wiki/Raid_(military)" title="Raid (military)">raiding</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> harmed Kuwait's economy, starting in the late 1920s.<sup id="cite_ref-do_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-do-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> International trading was one of Kuwait's main sources of income before oil.<sup id="cite_ref-do_39-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-do-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Kuwaiti merchants were mostly intermediary merchants.<sup id="cite_ref-do_39-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-do-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> As a result of the decline of European demand for goods from India and Africa, Kuwait's economy suffered. The decline in international trade resulted in an increase in gold smuggling by Kuwaiti ships to India.<sup id="cite_ref-do_39-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-do-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Some Kuwaiti merchant families became rich from this smuggling.<sup id="cite_ref-hist_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hist-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait's <a href="/wiki/Pearl" title="Pearl">pearl</a> industry also collapsed as a result of the worldwide economic depression.<sup id="cite_ref-hist_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hist-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> At its height, Kuwait's pearl industry had led the world's luxury market, regularly sending out between 750 and 800 ships to meet the European elite's desire for pearls.<sup id="cite_ref-hist_40-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hist-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> During the economic depression, luxuries like pearls were in little demand.<sup id="cite_ref-hist_40-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hist-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The Japanese invention of <a href="/wiki/Cultured_pearls" class="mw-redirect" title="Cultured pearls">cultured pearls</a> also contributed to the collapse of Kuwait's pearl industry.<sup id="cite_ref-hist_40-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hist-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Historian <a href="/wiki/Hanna_Batatu" title="Hanna Batatu">Hanna Batatu</a> explains how the British threatened to take the Kurdish area and Mosul out of Iraq provided that King Faisal granted Britain control of the oil in the region. In 1938 the Kuwaiti Legislative Council<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> unanimously approved a request for Kuwait's reintegration with Iraq. A year later an armed uprising which had raised the integration banner as its objective was put down by the British.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1962.E2.80.931982_.28Prosperity_and_growing_poverty.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1962–1982_(Prosperity_and_growing_poverty)">1962–1982 (Prosperity and growing poverty)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1962–1982 (Prosperity and growing poverty)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stamp_Kuwait_1957_15np.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Stamp_Kuwait_1957_15np.jpg/150px-Stamp_Kuwait_1957_15np.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Stamp_Kuwait_1957_15np.jpg/225px-Stamp_Kuwait_1957_15np.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Stamp_Kuwait_1957_15np.jpg/300px-Stamp_Kuwait_1957_15np.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="590" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stamp_Kuwait_1957_15np.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Postage stamp with portrait of <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a>, 1957</div></div></div>
<p>With the end of the world war, and increasing need for oil across the world, Kuwait experienced a period of prosperity driven by oil and its liberal atmosphere. The period of 1946-82 is often termed "the golden period of Kuwait" by western academics.<sup id="cite_ref-venezia_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-venezia-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pavilion_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pavilion-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-farid_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-farid-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> In popular discourse, the years between 1946 and 1982 are referred to as the "Golden Era".<sup id="cite_ref-venezia_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-venezia-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pavilion_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pavilion-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-farid_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-farid-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> However, Kuwaiti academics argue that this period was marked by benefits accruing only to the wealthier and connected ruling classes. It saw an increased presence of British, American and French citizens connected with the new oil industry, wealth transfer to people connected with the Emir, the creation of a new privileged upper class of educated Kuwaitis, bankers, and a vast majority of Kuwaitis living a life of penury. This resulted in a growing gulf between the wealthy minority and the majority of common citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-Farah_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Farah-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> In 1950, a major public-work programme began to enable Kuwaitis to enjoy a modern standard of living. By 1952, the country became the largest oil exporter in the Persian Gulf region. This massive growth attracted many foreign workers, especially from Palestine, India, and Egypt – with the latter being particularly political within the context of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Cold_War" title="Arab Cold War">Arab Cold War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> In June 1961, Kuwait became independent with the end of the <a href="/wiki/Sheikhdom_of_Kuwait#History_as_a_Protected_State_of_Britain" title="Sheikhdom of Kuwait">British protectorate</a> and the Sheikh <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_Al-Salim_Al-Sabah" title="Abdullah Al-Salim Al-Sabah">Abdullah Al-Salim Al-Sabah</a> became <a href="/wiki/Emir_of_Kuwait" title="Emir of Kuwait">Emir of Kuwait</a>. Kuwait's <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Kuwait" title="Public holidays in Kuwait">national day</a>, however, is celebrated on 25 February, the anniversary of the coronation of Sheikh Abdullah (it was originally celebrated on 19 June, the date of independence, but concerns over the summer heat caused the government to move it).<sup id="cite_ref-Fuller2004_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fuller2004-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Under the terms of the newly drafted <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Kuwait" title="Constitution of Kuwait">Constitution</a>, Kuwait held its first <a href="/wiki/Kuwaiti_parliamentary_election,_1963" class="mw-redirect" title="Kuwaiti parliamentary election, 1963">parliamentary elections in 1963</a>. Kuwait was the first of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_states_of_the_Persian_Gulf" title="Arab states of the Persian Gulf">Arab states of the Persian Gulf</a> to establish a constitution and parliament.
</p><p>In the 1960s and 1970s, Kuwait was considered by some as the most developed country in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-index_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-index-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait was the pioneer in the Middle East in diversifying its earnings away from oil exports.<sup id="cite_ref-swf_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-swf-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Investment_Authority" title="Kuwait Investment Authority">Kuwait Investment Authority</a> is the world's first sovereign wealth fund. From the 1970s onward, Kuwait scored highest of all Arab countries on the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-index_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-index-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_University" title="Kuwait University">Kuwait University</a> was established in 1966.<sup id="cite_ref-index_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-index-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait's <a href="/wiki/Kuwait#Theatre" title="Kuwait">theatre industry</a> was well known throughout the Arab world.<sup id="cite_ref-venezia_43-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-venezia-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-index_51-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-index-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> However, it also began to see the growth of plush <a href="/wiki/Gated_community" title="Gated community">gated properties</a>, wherein the interiors resembled western villas and the streets were filled with roads marked with potholes.<sup id="cite_ref-Farah_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Farah-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 1960s and 1970s, Kuwait's press was described as one of the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_press" title="Freedom of the press">freest in the world</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-review_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-review-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait was the pioneer in the literary renaissance in the Arab region.<sup id="cite_ref-pioneer_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pioneer-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> In 1958, <i><a href="/wiki/Al-Arabi_(magazine)" title="Al-Arabi (magazine)">Al-Arabi</a></i> magazine was first published.  The magazine went on to become the most popular magazine in the Arab world.<sup id="cite_ref-pioneer_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pioneer-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Many Arab writers moved to Kuwait because they enjoyed greater <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_expression" class="mw-redirect" title="Freedom of expression">freedom of expression</a> than elsewhere in the Arab world.<sup id="cite_ref-newsmedia_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newsmedia-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The Iraqi poet <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Matar" title="Ahmed Matar">Ahmed Matar</a> left Iraq in the 1970s to take refuge in the more liberal environment of Kuwait.
</p><p>Kuwaiti society embraced <a href="/wiki/Westernization" title="Westernization">liberal and Western attitudes</a> throughout the 1960s and 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> For example, most Kuwaiti women did not wear the <a href="/wiki/Hijab" title="Hijab">hijab</a> in the 1960s and 70s.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1982_to_present_day">1982 to present day</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1982 to present day">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jacckuwait.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Jacckuwait.jpg/220px-Jacckuwait.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Jacckuwait.jpg/330px-Jacckuwait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Jacckuwait.jpg/440px-Jacckuwait.jpg 2x" data-file-width="490" data-file-height="367" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jacckuwait.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sheikh_Jaber_Al-Ahmad_Cultural_Centre" title="Sheikh Jaber Al-Ahmad Cultural Centre">Sheikh Jaber Al-Ahmad Cultural Centre</a><sup id="cite_ref-alb_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alb-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>In the early 1980s, Kuwait experienced a major <a href="/wiki/Economic_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic crisis">economic crisis</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Souk_Al-Manakh_stock_market_crash" title="Souk Al-Manakh stock market crash">Souk Al-Manakh stock market crash</a> and <a href="/wiki/1980s_oil_glut" title="1980s oil glut">decrease in oil price</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Iraq_War" title="Iran–Iraq War">Iran–Iraq War</a>, Kuwait supported Iraq. Throughout the 1980s, there were several <a href="/wiki/Terrorism_in_Kuwait" title="Terrorism in Kuwait">terror attacks</a> in Kuwait, including the <a href="/wiki/1983_Kuwait_bombings" title="1983 Kuwait bombings">1983 Kuwait bombings</a>, hijacking of <a href="/wiki/1983_Kuwait_bombings#Aircraft_hijackings_(1984–1988)" title="1983 Kuwait bombings">several Kuwait Airways planes</a> and the attempted assassination of <a href="/wiki/Jaber_Al-Ahmad_Al-Sabah" title="Jaber Al-Ahmad Al-Sabah">Emir Jaber</a> in 1985. Kuwait was a regional hub of science and technology in the 1960s and 1970s up until the early 1980s; the scientific research sector significantly suffered due to the terror attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-s&amp;t_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-s&amp;t-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the Iran–Iraq War ended, Kuwait declined an Iraqi request to forgive its US$65&#160;billion debt.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> An economic rivalry between the two countries ensued after Kuwait increased its oil production by 40 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-Gregory2004_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gregory2004-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Tensions between the two countries increased further in July 1990, after Iraq complained to <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a> claiming that Kuwait was stealing its oil from a field near the border by <a href="/wiki/Slant_drilling" class="mw-redirect" title="Slant drilling">slant drilling</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Rumaila_field" class="mw-redirect" title="Rumaila field">Rumaila field</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Gregory2004_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gregory2004-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 1990, Iraqi forces <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Kuwait" title="Invasion of Kuwait">invaded and annexed</a> Kuwait. After a series of failed diplomatic negotiations, the United States led a coalition to remove the Iraqi forces from Kuwait, in what became known as the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">Gulf War</a>. On 26 February 1991, the coalition succeeded in driving out the Iraqi forces. As they retreated, Iraqi forces carried out a <a href="/wiki/Kuwaiti_oil_fires" title="Kuwaiti oil fires">scorched earth</a> policy by setting oil wells on fire.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> During the Iraqi occupation, more than 1,000 Kuwaiti civilians were killed. In addition, more than 600 Kuwaitis went <a href="/wiki/Missing_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Missing people">missing</a> during Iraq's occupation;<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> remains of approximately 375 were found in mass graves in Iraq.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:POTD-September-5-2018.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/POTD-September-5-2018.jpg/220px-POTD-September-5-2018.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/POTD-September-5-2018.jpg/330px-POTD-September-5-2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/POTD-September-5-2018.jpg/440px-POTD-September-5-2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2600" data-file-height="1733" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:POTD-September-5-2018.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> welcomes the Amir of Kuwait <a href="/wiki/Sabah_Al-Ahmad_Al-Jaber_Al-Sabah" title="Sabah Al-Ahmad Al-Jaber Al-Sabah">Sabah Al-Ahmad Al-Jaber Al-Sabah</a> to the White House, 2018</div></div></div>
<p>In March 2003, Kuwait became the springboard for the US-led <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Iraq" class="mw-redirect" title="Invasion of Iraq">invasion of Iraq</a>. Upon the death of the Emir Jaber in January 2006, <a href="/wiki/Saad_Al-Sabah" class="mw-redirect" title="Saad Al-Sabah">Saad Al-Sabah</a> succeeded him but was removed nine days later by the Kuwaiti parliament due to his ailing health. <a href="/wiki/Sabah_Al-Sabah" class="mw-redirect" title="Sabah Al-Sabah">Sabah Al-Sabah</a> was sworn in as Emir.
</p><p>From 2001 to 2009, Kuwait had the highest <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> ranking in the Arab world.<sup id="cite_ref-kuna_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kuna-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HDI2_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HDI2-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HDI21_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HDI21-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HDI1_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HDI1-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> In 2005, women won the right to vote and run in elections. In 2014 and 2015, Kuwait was ranked first among Arab countries in the <a href="/wiki/Global_Gender_Gap_Report" title="Global Gender Gap Report">Global Gender Gap Report</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hgh_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hgh-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wid_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wid-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wef_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wef-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sabah_Al_Ahmad_Sea_City" title="Sabah Al Ahmad Sea City">Sabah Al Ahmad Sea City</a> was inaugurated in mid 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-twf_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-twf-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Amiri_Diwan_of_Kuwait" title="Amiri Diwan of Kuwait">Amiri Diwan</a> is currently developing the new <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_National_Cultural_District" title="Kuwait National Cultural District">Kuwait National Cultural District</a> (KNCD), which comprises <a href="/wiki/Sheikh_Abdullah_Al_Salem_Cultural_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheikh Abdullah Al Salem Cultural Centre">Sheikh Abdullah Al Salem Cultural Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheikh_Jaber_Al_Ahmad_Cultural_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheikh Jaber Al Ahmad Cultural Centre">Sheikh Jaber Al Ahmad Cultural Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Shaheed_Park" title="Al Shaheed Park">Al Shaheed Park</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Al_Salam_Palace_(Kuwait)" title="Al Salam Palace (Kuwait)">Al Salam Palace</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kncd_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kncd-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kncd2_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kncd2-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> With a capital cost of more than US$1&#160;billion, the project is one of the largest cultural investments in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-kncd_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kncd-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> In November 2016, the Sheikh Jaber Al Ahmad Cultural Centre opened.<sup id="cite_ref-alb_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alb-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> It is the largest cultural centre in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-omnd_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-omnd-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-opsc_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-opsc-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> The Kuwait National Cultural District is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Global_Cultural_Districts_Network" title="Global Cultural Districts Network">Global Cultural Districts Network</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gcdn_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gcdn-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> In 2016 Kuwait commenced a new national development plan, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait_Vision_2035&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kuwait Vision 2035 (page does not exist)">Kuwait Vision 2035</a>, including plans to diversify the economy and become less dependent on oil.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Kuwait" title="Culture of Kuwait">Culture of Kuwait</a></div>
<p>Kuwaiti <a href="/wiki/Popular_culture" title="Popular culture">popular culture</a>, in the form of theatre, radio, music, and television soap opera, flourishes and is even exported to neighboring states.<sup id="cite_ref-cliv_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cliv-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Within the Persian Gulf Arab states, the culture of Kuwait is the closest to the culture of <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>; this is evident in the close association between the two states in theatrical productions and soap operas.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Society">Society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Kuwaiti society is markedly more <a href="/wiki/Open_society" title="Open society">open</a> than other Persian Gulf Arab societies.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Kuwaiti citizens are ethnically diverse, consisting of both Arabs and <a href="/wiki/%27Ajam_of_Kuwait" title="&#39;Ajam of Kuwait">Persians ('Ajam)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-venez2_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-venez2-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait stands out in the region as the most liberal in empowering women in the public sphere.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Kuwait" title="Women in Kuwait">Kuwaiti women</a> outnumber men in the workforce.<sup id="cite_ref-gnw_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gnw-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Kuwaiti political scientist Ghanim Alnajjar sees these qualities as a manifestation of Kuwaiti society as a whole, whereby in the Persian Gulf region it is "the least strict about traditions".<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television_and_theatre">Television and theatre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Television and theatre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Kuwait" title="Cinema of Kuwait">Cinema of Kuwait</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Abdulhussain_Abdulredha_2009_(cropped)_version.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Abdulhussain_Abdulredha_2009_%28cropped%29_version.jpg/220px-Abdulhussain_Abdulredha_2009_%28cropped%29_version.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="243" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/67/Abdulhussain_Abdulredha_2009_%28cropped%29_version.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="241" data-file-height="266" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Abdulhussain_Abdulredha_2009_(cropped)_version.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Abdulhussain_Abdulredha" title="Abdulhussain Abdulredha">Abdulhussain Abdulredha</a>, the most prominent Kuwaiti actor.</div></div></div>
<p>Kuwait's television drama industry tops other Persian Gulf drama industries and produces a minimum of fifteen serials annually.<sup id="cite_ref-omn_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-omn-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ahma_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ahma-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait is the production centre of the Persian Gulf television drama and comedy scene.<sup id="cite_ref-ahma_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ahma-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Most Persian Gulf television drama and comedy productions are filmed in Kuwait.<sup id="cite_ref-ahma_93-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ahma-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Kuwaiti soap operas are the most-watched soap operas from the Gulf region.<sup id="cite_ref-omn_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-omn-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fattah_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fattah-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Soap operas are most popular during the time of <a href="/wiki/Ramadan" title="Ramadan">Ramadan</a>, when families gather to break their fast.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Although usually performed in the <a href="/wiki/Kuwaiti_Arabic" title="Kuwaiti Arabic">Kuwaiti dialect</a>, they have been shown with success as far away as <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait is frequently dubbed the "<a href="/wiki/Hollywood" title="Hollywood">Hollywood</a> of the Gulf" due to the popularity of its television soap operas and theatre.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kuwait is known for its home-grown tradition of <a href="/wiki/Theatre" title="Theatre">theatre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hammond_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hammond-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait is the only country in the Persian Gulf with a theatrical tradition.<sup id="cite_ref-hammond_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hammond-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> The theatrical movement in Kuwait constitutes a major part of the country's cultural life.<sup id="cite_ref-theat_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theat-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Theatrical activities in Kuwait began in the 1920s when the first spoken dramas were released.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Theatre activities are still popular today.<sup id="cite_ref-theat_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theat-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Abdulhussain_Abdulredha" title="Abdulhussain Abdulredha">Abdulhussain Abdulredha</a> is the most prominent actor.
</p><p>Kuwait is the main centre of <a href="/wiki/Scenography" title="Scenography">scenographic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Performing_arts_education" title="Performing arts education">theatrical training</a> in the Persian Gulf region.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thae_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thae-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> In 1973, the Higher Institute of Theatrical Arts was founded by the government to provide <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">higher education</a> in theatrical arts.<sup id="cite_ref-thae_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thae-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> The institute has several divisions. Many actors have graduated from the institute, such as <a href="/wiki/Souad_Abdullah" title="Souad Abdullah">Souad Abdullah</a>, Mohammed Khalifa, <a href="/wiki/Mansour_Al-Mansour" title="Mansour Al-Mansour">Mansour Al-Mansour</a>, along with a number of prominent critics such as <a href="/wiki/Ismail_Fahd_Ismail" title="Ismail Fahd Ismail">Ismail Fahd Ismail</a>.
</p><p>Theatre in Kuwait is subsidized by the government, previously by the Ministry of Social Affairs and now by the National Council for Culture, Arts, and Letters (NCCAL).<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Every urban district has a public theatre.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> The public theatre in <a href="/wiki/Salmiya" title="Salmiya">Salmiya</a> is named after Abdulhussain Abdulredha.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">Arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Art_of_Kuwait" title="Art of Kuwait">Art of Kuwait</a></div>
<p>Kuwait has the oldest <a href="/wiki/Modern_arts" class="mw-redirect" title="Modern arts">modern arts</a> movement in the Arabian Peninsula.<sup id="cite_ref-movemnt_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-movemnt-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Beginning in 1936, Kuwait was the first Persian Gulf country to grant scholarships in the arts.<sup id="cite_ref-movemnt_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-movemnt-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> The Kuwaiti artist <a href="/wiki/Mojeb_al-Dousari" title="Mojeb al-Dousari">Mojeb al-Dousari</a> was the earliest recognized <a href="/wiki/Visual_artist" class="mw-redirect" title="Visual artist">visual artist</a> in the Gulf region.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> He is regarded as the founder of <a href="/wiki/Portrait" title="Portrait">portrait</a> art in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> The Sultan Gallery was the first professional Arab art gallery in the Gulf.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kuwait is home to more than <a href="/wiki/Art_of_Kuwait#Art_galleries" title="Art of Kuwait">30 art galleries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> In recent years, Kuwait's contemporary art scene has boomed.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Khalifa_Al-Qattan" class="mw-redirect" title="Khalifa Al-Qattan">Khalifa Al-Qattan</a> was the first artist to hold a <a href="/wiki/Solo_exhibition" title="Solo exhibition">solo exhibition</a> in Kuwait. He founded a new art theory in the early 1960s known as "circulism".<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Other notable Kuwaiti artists include <a href="/wiki/Sami_Mohammad" title="Sami Mohammad">Sami Mohammad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thuraya_Al-Baqsami" title="Thuraya Al-Baqsami">Thuraya Al-Baqsami</a> and <a href="/wiki/Suzan_Bushnaq" title="Suzan Bushnaq">Suzan Bushnaq</a>.
</p><p>The government organizes various <a href="/wiki/Arts_festivals" class="mw-redirect" title="Arts festivals">arts festivals</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Al_Qurain_Cultural_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Qurain Cultural Festival">Al Qurain Cultural Festival</a> and Formative Arts Festival.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> The Kuwait International Biennial was inaugurated in 1967,<sup id="cite_ref-biennial_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biennial-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> more than 20 Arab and foreign countries have participated in the biennial.<sup id="cite_ref-biennial_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biennial-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Prominent participants include <a href="/wiki/Layla_Al-Attar" title="Layla Al-Attar">Layla Al-Attar</a>. In 2004, the Al Kharafi Biennial for Contemporary Arab Art was inaugurated.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Kuwait" title="Music of Kuwait">Music of Kuwait</a></div>
<p>Kuwait is the birthplace of various popular musical genres, such as <a href="/wiki/Sawt_(music)" title="Sawt (music)">sawt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kwq_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kwq-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Kuwaiti music has considerably influenced the music culture in other GCC countries.<sup id="cite_ref-rvo_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rvo-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kwq_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kwq-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Traditional Kuwaiti music is a reflection of the country's seafaring heritage,<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> which is known for genres such as <a href="/wiki/Fijiri" title="Fijiri">fijiri</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ya_Bahr_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ya_Bahr-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-qdl_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qdl-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait pioneered <a href="/wiki/Khaliji_(music)" title="Khaliji (music)">contemporary Khaliji music</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-shart_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shart-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pers_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pers-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-shartw_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shartw-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Kuwaitis were the first commercial recording artists in the Gulf region.<sup id="cite_ref-shart_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shart-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pers_136-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pers-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-shartw_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shartw-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> The first known Kuwaiti recordings were made between 1912 and 1915.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Sheikh_Jaber_Al-Ahmad_Cultural_Centre" title="Sheikh Jaber Al-Ahmad Cultural Centre">Sheikh Jaber Al-Ahmad Cultural Centre</a> contains the largest opera house in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait is home to various <a href="/wiki/Music_festivals" class="mw-redirect" title="Music festivals">music festivals</a>, including the International Music Festival hosted by the National Council for Culture, Arts and Letters (NCCAL).<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait has several academic institutions specializing in university-level <a href="/wiki/Music_education" title="Music education">music education</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ohiol_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohiol-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-soton_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-soton-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ohiocsw_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohiocsw-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> The Higher Institute of Musical Arts was established by the government to provide <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degrees" class="mw-redirect" title="Bachelor&#39;s degrees">bachelor's degrees</a> in music.<sup id="cite_ref-ohiol_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohiol-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-soton_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-soton-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ohiocsw_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohiocsw-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> In addition, the College of Basic Education offers bachelor's degrees in music education.<sup id="cite_ref-ohiol_142-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohiol-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-soton_143-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-soton-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ohiocsw_144-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohiocsw-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> The Institute of Musical Studies offers degrees equivalent to <a href="/wiki/Secondary_school" title="Secondary school">secondary school</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ohiol_142-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohiol-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ohiocsw_144-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohiocsw-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-soton_143-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-soton-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kuwaiti_literature" title="Kuwaiti literature">Kuwaiti literature</a></div>
<p>Kuwait has, in recent years, produced several prominent contemporary writers such as <a href="/wiki/Ismail_Fahd_Ismail" title="Ismail Fahd Ismail">Ismail Fahd Ismail</a>, author of over twenty novels and numerous short story collections.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> There is also evidence that Kuwaiti literature has long been interactive with English and French literature.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_in_Kuwait" title="List of museums in Kuwait">List of museums in Kuwait</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Beitalsadu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Beitalsadu.jpg/220px-Beitalsadu.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Beitalsadu.jpg/330px-Beitalsadu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Beitalsadu.jpg/440px-Beitalsadu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="634" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Beitalsadu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sadu_House" title="Sadu House">Sadu House</a></div></div></div>
<p>The new <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_National_Cultural_District" title="Kuwait National Cultural District">Kuwait National Cultural District</a> (KNCD) consists of various cultural venues including <a href="/wiki/Sheikh_Abdullah_Al_Salem_Cultural_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheikh Abdullah Al Salem Cultural Centre">Sheikh Abdullah Al Salem Cultural Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheikh_Jaber_Al_Ahmad_Cultural_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheikh Jaber Al Ahmad Cultural Centre">Sheikh Jaber Al Ahmad Cultural Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Shaheed_Park" title="Al Shaheed Park">Al Shaheed Park</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Al_Salam_Palace_(Kuwait)" title="Al Salam Palace (Kuwait)">Al Salam Palace</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kncd_76-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kncd-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kncd2_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kncd2-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> With a capital cost of more than US$1&#160;billion, it is one of the largest cultural districts in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-kncd_76-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kncd-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> The Abdullah Salem Cultural Centre is the largest museum complex in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> The Kuwait National Cultural District is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Global_Cultural_Districts_Network" title="Global Cultural Districts Network">Global Cultural Districts Network</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gcdn_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gcdn-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Several Kuwaiti museums are devoted to <a href="/wiki/Islamic_art" title="Islamic art">Islamic art</a>, most notably the <a href="/wiki/Tareq_Rajab_Museum" title="Tareq Rajab Museum">Tareq Rajab Museums</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dar_al_Athar_al_Islamiyyah" title="Dar al Athar al Islamiyyah">Dar al Athar al Islamiyyah</a> cultural centres.<sup id="cite_ref-modmus_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-modmus-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> The Dar al Athar al Islamiyyah cultural centres include education wings, conservation labs, and research libraries.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dai_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dai-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> There are several <a href="/wiki/Libraries" class="mw-redirect" title="Libraries">art libraries</a> in Kuwait.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dai_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dai-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Khalifa_Al-Qattan" class="mw-redirect" title="Khalifa Al-Qattan">Khalifa Al-Qattan</a>'s Mirror House is the most popular art museum in Kuwait.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> Many museums in Kuwait are private enterprises.<sup id="cite_ref-trans_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trans-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-modmus_149-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-modmus-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> In contrast to the top-down approach in other Gulf states, museum development in Kuwait reflects a greater sense of civic identity and demonstrates the strength of civil society in Kuwait, which has produced many independent cultural enterprises.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-modmus_149-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-modmus-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-trans_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trans-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sadu_House" title="Sadu House">Sadu House</a> is among Kuwait's most important cultural institutions. <a href="/wiki/Bait_Al-Othman_Museum" title="Bait Al-Othman Museum">Bait Al-Othman</a> is the largest museum specializing in Kuwait's history. <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Scientific_Center" title="Kuwait Scientific Center">The Scientific Center</a> is one of the largest science museums in the Middle East. The <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Modern_Art_(Kuwait)" title="Museum of Modern Art (Kuwait)">Museum of Modern Art</a> showcases the history of modern art in Kuwait and the region.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_National_Museum" title="Kuwait National Museum">National Museum</a>, established in 1983, has been described as "underused and overlooked".<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is the most popular sport in Kuwait. The <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Football_Association" title="Kuwait Football Association">Kuwait Football Association</a> (KFA) is the governing body of football in Kuwait. The KFA organises the <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_national_football_team" title="Kuwait national football team">men's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Kuwait women&#39;s national football team">women's</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Futsal" title="Futsal">futsal</a> national teams. The <a href="/wiki/Kuwaiti_Premier_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Kuwaiti Premier League">Kuwaiti Premier League</a> is the top league of Kuwaiti football, featuring eighteen teams. They have been the champions of the <a href="/wiki/1980_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="1980 AFC Asian Cup">1980 AFC Asian Cup</a>, runners-up of the <a href="/wiki/1976_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="1976 AFC Asian Cup">1976 AFC Asian Cup</a>, and have taken third place of the <a href="/wiki/1984_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="1984 AFC Asian Cup">1984 AFC Asian Cup</a>. Kuwait has also been to one FIFA World Cup, in <a href="/wiki/1982_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1982 FIFA World Cup">1982</a>; they drew 1–1 with <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia_national_football_team" title="Czechoslovakia national football team">Czechoslovakia</a> before losing to <a href="/wiki/France_national_football_team" title="France national football team">France</a> and <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a>, failing to advance from the first round. Kuwait is home to many football clubs including <a href="/wiki/Al-Arabi_SC_(Kuwait)" title="Al-Arabi SC (Kuwait)">Al-Arabi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fahaheel_(football_club)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fahaheel (football club)">Al-Fahaheel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Jahra_(football_club)" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Jahra (football club)">Al-Jahra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Kuwait_Kaifan" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Kuwait Kaifan">Al-Kuwait</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Naser_Sporting_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Naser Sporting Club">Al-Naser</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Salmiya_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Salmiya Club">Al-Salmiya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al-Shabab_(Kuwait)" class="mw-redirect" title="Al-Shabab (Kuwait)">Al-Shabab</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Qadsia_Kuwait" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Qadsia Kuwait">Al Qadsia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Yarmouk_(football_club)" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Yarmouk (football club)">Al-Yarmouk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Kazma_Kuwait" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Kazma Kuwait">Kazma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khaitan" title="Khaitan">Khaitan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sulaibikhat" title="Sulaibikhat">Sulaibikhat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sahel_(Kuwaiti_football_club)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sahel (Kuwaiti football club)">Sahel</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tadamon,_Kuwait" class="mw-redirect" title="Tadamon, Kuwait">Tadamon</a>. The biggest football rivalry in Kuwait is between <a href="/wiki/Al-Arabi_SC_(Kuwait)" title="Al-Arabi SC (Kuwait)">Al-Arabi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Al_Qadsia_Kuwait" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Qadsia Kuwait">Al Qadsia</a>.
</p><p>Basketball is one of the country's most popular sports. The <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_national_basketball_team" title="Kuwait national basketball team">Kuwait national basketball team</a> is governed by the Kuwait Basketball Association (KBA). Kuwait made its international debut in 1959. The national team has been to the <a href="/wiki/FIBA_Asian_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="FIBA Asian Championship">FIBA Asian Championship</a> in basketball eleven times. The <a href="/wiki/Kuwaiti_Division_I_Basketball_League" title="Kuwaiti Division I Basketball League">Kuwaiti Division I Basketball League</a> is the highest professional basketball league in Kuwait. <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_national_cricket_team" title="Kuwait national cricket team">Cricket in Kuwait</a> is governed by the <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Cricket_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="Kuwait Cricket Association">Kuwait Cricket Association</a>. Other growing sports include <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_in_Kuwait" title="Rugby union in Kuwait">rugby union</a>. <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_national_handball_team" title="Kuwait national handball team">Handball</a> is widely considered to be the national icon of Kuwait, although football is more popular among the overall population.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Kuwait_national_ice_hockey_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Kuwait national ice hockey team">Ice hockey in Kuwait</a> is governed by the <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Ice_Hockey_Association" title="Kuwait Ice Hockey Association">Kuwait Ice Hockey Association</a>. Kuwait first joined the <a href="/wiki/International_Ice_Hockey_Federation" title="International Ice Hockey Federation">International Ice Hockey Federation</a> in 1985, but was expelled in 1992 due to a lack of ice hockey activity.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait was re-admitted into the IIHF in May 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, Kuwait won the <a href="/wiki/IIHF_Challenge_Cup_of_Asia" title="IIHF Challenge Cup of Asia">IIHF Challenge Cup of Asia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kuwait_Liberation_Tower_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Kuwait_Liberation_Tower_cropped.jpg/150px-Kuwait_Liberation_Tower_cropped.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="209" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Kuwait_Liberation_Tower_cropped.jpg/225px-Kuwait_Liberation_Tower_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Kuwait_Liberation_Tower_cropped.jpg/300px-Kuwait_Liberation_Tower_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="835" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kuwait_Liberation_Tower_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 372 m tall <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Telecommunications_Tower" class="mw-redirect" title="Kuwait Telecommunications Tower">Kuwait Telecommunications Tower</a> (leftmost) is the main communication tower of Kuwait.</div></div></div>
<p>Kuwait's media is annually classified as "partly free" in the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_Press" class="mw-redirect" title="Freedom of Press">Freedom of Press</a> survey by Freedom House.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> Since 2005,<sup id="cite_ref-prfr_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prfr-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait has frequently earned the highest ranking of all Arab countries in the annual <a href="/wiki/Press_Freedom_Index" title="Press Freedom Index">Press Freedom Index</a> by Reporters Without Borders.<sup id="cite_ref-fanak_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fanak-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-isr_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-isr-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-indi_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indi-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-indextwo_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indextwo-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ofa_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ofa-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, 2011, 2013 and 2014, Kuwait surpassed <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> as the country with the greatest press freedom in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-fanak_167-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fanak-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-isr_168-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-isr-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-indi_169-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indi-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-indextwo_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indextwo-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ofa_174-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ofa-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait is also frequently ranked as the Arab country with the greatest press freedom in Freedom House's annual Freedom of Press survey.<sup id="cite_ref-lead_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lead-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kuwait produces more <a href="/wiki/List_of_newspapers_in_Kuwait" title="List of newspapers in Kuwait">newspapers and magazines</a> per capita than its neighbors.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> There are limits to Kuwait's press freedom; while criticism of the government and ruling family members is permitted, Kuwait's constitution criminalizes criticism of the Emir.
</p><p>The state-owned <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_News_Agency" title="Kuwait News Agency">Kuwait News Agency</a> (KUNA) is the largest media house in the country. The Ministry of Information regulates the media industry in Kuwait.
</p><p>Kuwait has 15 satellite television channels, of which four are controlled by the Ministry of Information. State-owned <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Television" title="Kuwait Television">Kuwait Television</a> (KTV) offered first colored broadcast in 1974 and operates five television channels. Government-funded Radio Kuwait also offers daily informative programming in several foreign languages including <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Farsi" class="mw-redirect" title="Farsi">Farsi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a>, and English on the <a href="/wiki/AM_broadcasting" title="AM broadcasting">AM</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shortwave" class="mw-redirect" title="Shortwave">SW</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Kuwait" title="Politics of Kuwait">Politics of Kuwait</a>, <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Kuwait" title="Government of Kuwait">Government of Kuwait</a>, and <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Kuwait" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Kuwait">National Assembly of Kuwait</a></div>
<p>Kuwait is a constitutional emirate with a <a href="/wiki/Semi-democracy" title="Semi-democracy">semi-democratic</a> political system.<sup id="cite_ref-wsjo_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsjo-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Emir_of_Kuwait" title="Emir of Kuwait">Emir</a> is the head of state. The hybrid political system is divided between an <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Kuwait)" title="National Assembly (Kuwait)">elected parliament</a> and <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Kuwait" title="Government of Kuwait">appointed government</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Kuwait" title="Constitution of Kuwait">Constitution of Kuwait</a> was promulgated in 1962. Kuwait is among the Middle East's freest countries in <a href="/wiki/Civil_liberties" title="Civil liberties">civil liberties</a> and political rights.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> rates the country as "Partly Free" in the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_in_the_World" title="Freedom in the World">Freedom in the World</a> survey.<sup id="cite_ref-FH2011_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FH2011-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">Political culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Political culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Kuwait" title="Constitution of Kuwait">Constitution of Kuwait</a> is considered as a liberal constitution in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Cooperation_Council" title="Gulf Cooperation Council">GCC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-lse_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lse-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> It guarantees a wide range of civil liberties and rights. In contrast to other states in the region, the political process largely respects constitutional provisions. Kuwait has a robust <a href="/wiki/Public_sphere" title="Public sphere">public sphere</a> and active <a href="/wiki/Civil_society" title="Civil society">civil society</a> with political and social organizations that are <a href="/wiki/Political_parties" class="mw-redirect" title="Political parties">parties</a> in all but name.<sup id="cite_ref-rubin_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rubin-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-greo_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greo-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> Professional groups like the <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Chamber_of_Commerce_and_Industry" title="Kuwait Chamber of Commerce and Industry">Chamber of Commerce</a> maintain their autonomy from the government.<sup id="cite_ref-rubin_192-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rubin-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-greo_193-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greo-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
