<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Utzon_Kuwait_National_Assembly.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Utzon_Kuwait_National_Assembly.jpg/220px-Utzon_Kuwait_National_Assembly.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Utzon_Kuwait_National_Assembly.jpg/330px-Utzon_Kuwait_National_Assembly.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Utzon_Kuwait_National_Assembly.jpg/440px-Utzon_Kuwait_National_Assembly.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3236" data-file-height="2068" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Utzon_Kuwait_National_Assembly.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_National_Assembly_Building" title="Kuwait National Assembly Building">Kuwait National Assembly Building</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Kuwait)" title="National Assembly (Kuwait)">National Assembly</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislature</a> and has oversight authority. The National Assembly consists of fifty elected members, who are chosen in elections held every four years. Since the parliament can conduct inquiries into government actions and pass motions of no confidence, <a href="/wiki/Checks_and_balances" class="mw-redirect" title="Checks and balances">checks and balances</a> are robust in Kuwait.<sup id="cite_ref-btf_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-btf-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> The parliament can be dissolved under a set of conditions based on constitutional provisions.<sup id="cite_ref-pogar_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pogar-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> The Constitutional Court and Emir both have the power to dissolve the parliament, although the Constitutional Court can invalidate the Emir's dissolution.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Executive_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive power">Executive power</a> is executed by the government. The Emir appoints the prime minister, who in turn chooses the ministers comprising the government. According to the constitution, at least one minister has to be an elected MP from the parliament. The parliament is often rigorous in holding the <a href="/wiki/Government_accountable" class="mw-redirect" title="Government accountable">government accountable</a>, government ministers are frequently interpellated and forced to resign.<sup id="cite_ref-pogar_195-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pogar-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-btf_194-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-btf-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait has more government accountability and transparency than other <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Cooperation_Council" title="Gulf Cooperation Council">GCC</a> countries.<sup id="cite_ref-rubin_192-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rubin-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judiciary</a> is nominally independent of the executive and the legislature, and the Constitutional Court is charged with ruling on the conformity of laws and decrees with the constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-pogar_195-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pogar-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> The judiciary's independence has come under question, although the Constitutional Court is widely regarded as one of the most judicially independent courts in the Arab world.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> The Constitutional Court has the power to dissolve the parliament and invalidate the Emir's decrees, as happened in 2013 when the dissolved 2009 parliament resumed its role.
</p><p>Kuwaiti women outnumber men in the workforce.<sup id="cite_ref-gnw_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gnw-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The political participation of <a href="/wiki/Kuwaiti_women" class="mw-redirect" title="Kuwaiti women">Kuwaiti women</a> has been limited,<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> although Kuwaiti women are among the most emancipated women in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>.  In 2014 and 2015, Kuwait was ranked first among Arab countries in the <a href="/wiki/Global_Gender_Gap_Report" title="Global Gender Gap Report">Global Gender Gap Report</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hgh_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hgh-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wid_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wid-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wef_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wef-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, 53% of Kuwaiti women participated in the labor force.<sup id="cite_ref-gend_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gend-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait has higher female citizen participation in the workforce than other GCC countries.<sup id="cite_ref-gnw_90-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gnw-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gend_198-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gend-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Political groups and parliamentary voting blocs exist, although most candidates run as independents. Once elected, many deputies form voting blocs in the National Assembly. Kuwaiti law does not recognize political parties.<sup id="cite_ref-cc_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cc-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> However, numerous political groups function as <i>de facto</i> political parties in elections, and there are blocs in the parliament. Major <i>de facto</i> political parties include the <a href="/wiki/National_Democratic_Alliance_(Kuwait)" title="National Democratic Alliance (Kuwait)">National Democratic Alliance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Popular_Action_Bloc" title="Popular Action Bloc">Popular Action Bloc</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hadas" title="Hadas">Hadas</a> (Kuwaiti <a href="/wiki/Muslim_Brotherhood" title="Muslim Brotherhood">Muslim Brotherhood</a>), <a href="/wiki/National_Islamic_Alliance" title="National Islamic Alliance">National Islamic Alliance</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Justice_and_Peace_Alliance" title="Justice and Peace Alliance">Justice and Peace Alliance</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_system">Legal system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Legal system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Legal_system_of_Kuwait" title="Legal system of Kuwait">Legal system of Kuwait</a></div>
<p>Kuwait follows the "<a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">civil law system</a>" modeled after the French legal system,<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait's legal system is largely secular.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hopkins_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hopkins-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sharia_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Sharia law">Sharia law</a> governs only <a href="/wiki/Family_law" title="Family law">family law</a> for Muslim residents,<sup id="cite_ref-hopkins_205-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hopkins-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> while non-Muslims in Kuwait have a secular family law. For the application of <a href="/wiki/Family_law" title="Family law">family law</a>, there are three separate court sections: <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dhimmi" title="Dhimmi">non-Muslim</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, Kuwait's legal system is a mix of <a href="/wiki/English_common_law" class="mw-redirect" title="English common law">English common law</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_civil_law" class="mw-redirect" title="French civil law">French civil law</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Civil_Code" title="Egyptian Civil Code">Egyptian civil law</a> and Islamic law.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Court_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Court system">court system</a> in Kuwait is secular.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ipo_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipo-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> Unlike other <a href="/wiki/Arab_states_of_the_Persian_Gulf" title="Arab states of the Persian Gulf">Arab states of the Persian Gulf</a>, Kuwait does not have Sharia courts.<sup id="cite_ref-ipo_211-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipo-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> Sections of the civil court system administer family law.<sup id="cite_ref-ipo_211-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipo-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait has the most secular <a href="/wiki/Commercial_law" title="Commercial law">commercial law</a> in the Gulf.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> The parliament criminalized alcohol consumption in 1983.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait's <a href="/wiki/Code_of_Personal_Status_(Kuwait)" title="Code of Personal Status (Kuwait)">Code of Personal Status</a> was promulgated in 1984.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Kuwait" title="Human rights in Kuwait">Human rights in Kuwait</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Kuwait" title="Human rights in Kuwait">Human rights in Kuwait</a> has been the subject of criticism, particularly regarding <a href="/wiki/Migrant_workers_in_the_Gulf_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Migrant workers in the Gulf region">foreign workers' rights</a>. Expatriates account for 70% of Kuwait's total population. The <a href="/wiki/Kafala_system" title="Kafala system">kafala system</a> leaves foreign workers prone to exploitation. Kuwait has the most liberal labor laws in the GCC.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> As a result, the <a href="/wiki/International_Labour_Organization" title="International Labour Organization">International Labour Organization</a> (<a href="/wiki/ILO" class="mw-redirect" title="ILO">ILO</a>) removed Kuwait from the list of countries violating workers rights.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> Male <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">homosexuality</a> is <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Kuwait" title="LGBT rights in Kuwait">illegal in Kuwait</a> and punishable by up to 6 years in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kuwaiti activist and blogger <a href="/wiki/Hamad_al-Naqi" title="Hamad al-Naqi">Hamad al-Naqi</a>, who is a Kuwaiti <a href="/wiki/Shi%27ite" class="mw-redirect" title="Shi&#39;ite">Shi'ite</a>, was sentenced to 10 years in prison for "blasphemous tweets" and criticizing neighboring Saudi and Bahraini monarchs.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> designated al-Naqi a <a href="/wiki/Prisoner_of_conscience" title="Prisoner of conscience">prisoner of conscience</a> and called for his immediate and unconditional release.<sup id="cite_ref-AI_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AI-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of 2009, 20% of the youth in juvenile centres have dyslexia, as compared to the 6% of the general population.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> Data from a 1993 study found that there is a higher rate of psychiatric morbidity in Kuwaiti prisons than in the general population.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Kuwait" title="Foreign relations of Kuwait">Foreign relations of Kuwait</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Diplomatic_missions_of_Kuwait.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Diplomatic_missions_of_Kuwait.png/400px-Diplomatic_missions_of_Kuwait.png" decoding="async" width="400" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Diplomatic_missions_of_Kuwait.png/600px-Diplomatic_missions_of_Kuwait.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Diplomatic_missions_of_Kuwait.png/800px-Diplomatic_missions_of_Kuwait.png 2x" data-file-width="1425" data-file-height="625" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Diplomatic_missions_of_Kuwait.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Location of diplomatic missions of Kuwait: <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ED1C24; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Kuwait</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #000080; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Embassy</div></div></div></div>
<p>Foreign affairs relations of Kuwait is handled at the level of the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Kuwait)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Kuwait)">Ministry of Foreign Affairs</a>. The first foreign affairs department bureau was established in 1961. Kuwait became the 111th member state of the United Nations in May 1963. It is a long-standing member of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cooperation_Council_for_the_Arab_States_of_the_Gulf" class="mw-redirect" title="Cooperation Council for the Arab States of the Gulf">Cooperation Council for the Arab States of the Gulf</a>.
</p><p>Before the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">Gulf War</a>, Kuwait was the only "pro-<a href="/wiki/Soviet" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet">Soviet</a>" state in the Persian Gulf region.<sup id="cite_ref-russ_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-russ-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait acted as a conduit for the Soviets to the other Arab states of the Persian Gulf, and Kuwait was used to demonstrate the benefits of a pro-Soviet stance.<sup id="cite_ref-russ_223-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-russ-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> In July 1987, Kuwait refused to allow U.S. military bases in its territory.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> As a result of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">Gulf War</a>, Kuwait's relations with the U.S. have improved (<a href="/wiki/Major_non-NATO_ally" title="Major non-NATO ally">Major non-NATO ally</a>) and currently hosts thousands of <a href="/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces" title="United States Armed Forces">US military personnel</a> and contractors within active U.S. facilities. Kuwait is also a major ally of <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations" title="Association of Southeast Asian Nations">ASEAN</a>, while enjoying good relationship with <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, establishing cooperation model in numerous fields.<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto1_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> According to Kuwaiti officials, Kuwait is the largest Arab investor in <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, especially in the <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz" title="Mercedes-Benz">Mercedes-Benz</a> company.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Kuwait" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Kuwait">Military of Kuwait</a> traces its original roots to the Kuwaiti cavalrymen and infantrymen that used to protect Kuwait and its wall since the early 1900s. These cavalrymen and infantrymen formed the defense and security forces in metropolitan areas; charged with protecting outposts outside the wall of Kuwait.
</p><p>The Military of Kuwait consists of several joint defense forces. The governing bodies are the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defense_(Kuwait)" title="Ministry of Defense (Kuwait)">Kuwait Ministry of Defense</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Interior_(Kuwait)" title="Ministry of Interior (Kuwait)">Kuwait Ministry of Interior</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_National_Guard" title="Kuwait National Guard">Kuwait National Guard</a> and the Kuwait Fire Service Directorate. The <a href="/wiki/Emir_of_Kuwait" title="Emir of Kuwait">Emir of Kuwait</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">commander-in-chief</a> of all defense forces by default. Even in the most adverse of all times such as a war, the military is not allowed to make a single move without the Emir's consent.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Governorates_of_Kuwait" title="Governorates of Kuwait">Governorates of Kuwait</a> and <a href="/wiki/Areas_of_Kuwait" title="Areas of Kuwait">Areas of Kuwait</a></div>
<div class="floatright"><a href="/wiki/File:Kuwait_governorates_english.png" class="image"><img alt="Kuwait governorates english.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Kuwait_governorates_english.png/180px-Kuwait_governorates_english.png" decoding="async" width="180" height="171" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Kuwait_governorates_english.png/270px-Kuwait_governorates_english.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Kuwait_governorates_english.png/360px-Kuwait_governorates_english.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="476" /></a></div>
<p>Kuwait is divided into <a href="/wiki/Governorates_of_Kuwait" title="Governorates of Kuwait">six governorates</a>. The governorates are further <a href="/wiki/Areas_of_Kuwait" title="Areas of Kuwait">subdivided into areas</a>.
</p>
<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Al_Asimah_Governorate_(Kuwait)" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Asimah Governorate (Kuwait)">Al Asimah</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hawalli_Governorate" title="Hawalli Governorate">Hawalli</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Farwaniya_Governorate" title="Farwaniya Governorate">Farwaniya</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mubarak_Al-Kabeer_Governorate" title="Mubarak Al-Kabeer Governorate">Mubarak Al-Kabeer</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ahmadi_Governorate" title="Ahmadi Governorate">Ahmadi</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jahra_Governorate" title="Jahra Governorate">Jahra</a></li></ol>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Kuwait" title="Geography of Kuwait">Geography of Kuwait</a> and <a href="/wiki/Environmental_issues_in_Kuwait" title="Environmental issues in Kuwait">Environmental issues in Kuwait</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Satellite_image_of_Kuwait_in_November_2001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Satellite_image_of_Kuwait_in_November_2001.jpg/220px-Satellite_image_of_Kuwait_in_November_2001.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="203" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Satellite_image_of_Kuwait_in_November_2001.jpg/330px-Satellite_image_of_Kuwait_in_November_2001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Satellite_image_of_Kuwait_in_November_2001.jpg/440px-Satellite_image_of_Kuwait_in_November_2001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="762" data-file-height="703" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Satellite_image_of_Kuwait_in_November_2001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A satellite image of Kuwait reveals its desert topography.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kuwait_pol_06.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Kuwait_pol_06.jpg/220px-Kuwait_pol_06.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="252" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Kuwait_pol_06.jpg/330px-Kuwait_pol_06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Kuwait_pol_06.jpg/440px-Kuwait_pol_06.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1009" data-file-height="1155" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kuwait_pol_06.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kuwait shares land borders with Iraq and Saudi Arabia, and maritime borders with Iraq, Saudi Arabia, and Iran.</div></div></div>
<p>Located in the north-east corner of the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">Arabian Peninsula</a>, Kuwait is one of the smallest countries in the world in terms of land area. Kuwait lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/28th_parallel_north" title="28th parallel north">28°</a> and <a href="/wiki/31st_parallel_north" title="31st parallel north">31° N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/46th_meridian_east" title="46th meridian east">46°</a> and <a href="/wiki/49th_meridian_east" title="49th meridian east">49° E</a>. The flat, sandy <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Desert" title="Arabian Desert">Arabian Desert</a> covers most of Kuwait. Kuwait is generally low lying, with the highest point being 306&#160;m (1,004&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Above_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above sea level">above sea level</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kuwait has <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Kuwait" title="List of islands of Kuwait">nine islands</a>, all of which, with the exception of <a href="/wiki/Failaka_Island" title="Failaka Island">Failaka Island</a>, are uninhabited.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> With an area of 860&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (330&#160;sq&#160;mi), the <a href="/wiki/Bubiyan_Island" title="Bubiyan Island">Bubiyan</a> is the largest island in Kuwait and is connected to the rest of the country by a 2,380-metre-long (7,808&#160;ft) bridge.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> 0.6% of Kuwaiti land area is considered arable<sup id="cite_ref-cia_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> with sparse vegetation found along its 499-kilometre-long (310&#160;mi) coastline.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_City" title="Kuwait City">Kuwait City</a> is located on <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Bay" title="Kuwait Bay">Kuwait Bay</a>, a natural deep-water harbor.
</p><p>Kuwait's <a href="/wiki/Burgan_field" title="Burgan field">Burgan field</a> has a total capacity of approximately 70 billion barrels (1.1<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">×</span>10<sup>10</sup>&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of proven oil reserves. During the 1991 <a href="/wiki/Kuwaiti_oil_fires" title="Kuwaiti oil fires">Kuwaiti oil fires</a>, more than 500 oil lakes were created covering a combined surface area of about 35.7&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (13.8&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> The resulting soil contamination due to oil and soot accumulation had made eastern and south-eastern parts of Kuwait uninhabitable. Sand and oil residue had reduced large parts of the Kuwaiti desert to semi-asphalt surfaces.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> The oil spills during the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">Gulf War</a> also drastically affected Kuwait's marine resources.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Kuwait" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of Kuwait">Climate of Kuwait</a></div>
<p>The spring season in March is warm with occasional thunderstorms. The frequent winds from the northwest are cold in winter and hot in summer. Southeasterly damp winds spring up between July and October. Hot and dry south winds prevail in spring and early summer. The shamal, a northwesterly wind common during June and July, causes dramatic sandstorms.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> Summers in Kuwait are some of the hottest on earth (like <a href="/wiki/Ahvaz" title="Ahvaz">Ahvaz</a>). The highest recorded temperature was 53.9&#160;°C (129.0&#160;°F) at <a href="/wiki/Mitribah" title="Mitribah">Mitribah</a> on 21 July 2016, which is the highest temperature recorded in Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait experiences colder winters than other GCC countries because of its location in a northern position near Iraq and Iran.
</p><p>In 2014 Kuwait was the third country in the world in term of <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_carbon_dioxide_emissions_per_capita" title="List of countries by carbon dioxide emissions per capita">CO2 per capita emissions</a> after <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a> according to the World Bank.<sup id="cite_ref-test_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-test-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> On average, every single inhabitant released that year 25.2 metric tons of CO2 in the atmosphere. In comparison, the world average was 5.0 tons per capita the same year.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_parks">National parks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: National parks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>At present, there are five <a href="/wiki/Protected_areas" class="mw-redirect" title="Protected areas">protected areas</a> in Kuwait recognized by the <a href="/wiki/IUCN" class="mw-redirect" title="IUCN">IUCN</a>. In response to Kuwait becoming the <a href="/wiki/List_of_parties_to_the_Ramsar_Convention" title="List of parties to the Ramsar Convention">169th signatory</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Ramsar_Convention" title="Ramsar Convention">Ramsar Convention</a>, Bubyan island's Mubarak al-Kabeer reserve was designated as the country's first Wetland of International Importance.<sup id="cite_ref-ramsar_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ramsar-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> The 50,948&#160;ha reserve consists of small lagoons and shallow <a href="/wiki/Saltmarsh" class="mw-redirect" title="Saltmarsh">salt marshes</a> and is important as a stop-over for migrating birds on two migration routes.<sup id="cite_ref-ramsar_237-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ramsar-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> The reserve is home to the world's largest breeding colony of <a href="/wiki/Crab-plover" title="Crab-plover">crab-plover</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ramsar_237-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ramsar-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Kuwait" title="Wildlife of Kuwait">Wildlife of Kuwait</a></div>
<p>More than 363 species of birds were recorded in Kuwait, 18 species of which breed in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-bsc-eoc_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bsc-eoc-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait is situated at the crossroads of several major bird migration routes and between two and three million birds pass each year.<sup id="cite_ref-natstrat_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-natstrat-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> The marshes in northern Kuwait and Jahra have become increasingly important as a refuge for passage migrants.<sup id="cite_ref-natstrat_239-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-natstrat-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> Kuwaiti islands are important breeding areas for four species of <a href="/wiki/Tern" title="Tern">tern</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Socotra_cormorant" title="Socotra cormorant">socotra cormorant</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-natstrat_239-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-natstrat-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kuwait's marine and littoral ecosystems contain the bulk of the country's biodiversity heritage.<sup id="cite_ref-natstrat_239-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-natstrat-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> Twenty eight species of mammal are found in Kuwait; animals such as gerboa, desert rabbits and <a href="/wiki/Hedgehog" title="Hedgehog">hedgehogs</a> are common in the desert.<sup id="cite_ref-natstrat_239-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-natstrat-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> Large carnivores, such as the <a href="/wiki/Wolf" title="Wolf">wolf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caracal" title="Caracal">caracal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jackal" title="Jackal">jackal</a>, are not found.<sup id="cite_ref-natstrat_239-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-natstrat-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> Among the endangered mammalian species are the <a href="/wiki/Red_fox" title="Red fox">red fox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wild_cat" class="mw-redirect" title="Wild cat">wild cat</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-natstrat_239-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-natstrat-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> Causes for wildlife extinction are habitat destruction and extensive unregulated hunting.<sup id="cite_ref-natstrat_239-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-natstrat-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> Forty reptile species have been recorded although none are endemic to Kuwait.<sup id="cite_ref-natstrat_239-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-natstrat-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_and_sanitation">Water and sanitation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Water and sanitation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kuwait_Water_Towers.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Kuwait_Water_Towers.jpg/250px-Kuwait_Water_Towers.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="183" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Kuwait_Water_Towers.jpg/375px-Kuwait_Water_Towers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Kuwait_Water_Towers.jpg/500px-Kuwait_Water_Towers.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1009" data-file-height="740" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kuwait_Water_Towers.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Water_Towers" title="Kuwait Water Towers">Kuwait Water Towers</a> in Kuwait City</div></div></div>
<p>Kuwait does not have any permanent rivers. It does have some <a href="/wiki/Wadi" title="Wadi">wadis</a>, the most notable of which is <a href="/wiki/Wadi_Al-Batin" title="Wadi Al-Batin">Wadi Al-Batin</a> which forms the border between Kuwait and <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>.
</p><p>Kuwait relies on water <a href="/wiki/Desalination" title="Desalination">desalination</a> as a primary source of fresh water for drinking and domestic purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-scidi_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scidi-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fao_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fao-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> There are currently more than six desalination plants.<sup id="cite_ref-fao_241-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fao-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait was the first country in the world to use desalination to supply water for large-scale domestic use. The history of desalination in Kuwait dates back to 1951 when the first distillation plant was commissioned.<sup id="cite_ref-scidi_240-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scidi-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1965, the Kuwaiti government commissioned the Swedish engineering company of VBB (<a href="/wiki/Sweco" title="Sweco">Sweco</a>) to develop and implement a plan for a modern <a href="/wiki/Water-supply_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Water-supply system">water-supply system</a> for Kuwait City. The company built <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Water_Towers" title="Kuwait Water Towers">five groups of water towers</a>, thirty-one towers total, designed by its chief architect <a href="/wiki/Sune_Lindstr%C3%B6m" title="Sune Lindström">Sune Lindström</a>, called "the mushroom towers". For a sixth site, the Emir of Kuwait, Sheikh <a href="/wiki/Jaber_al-Ahmad_al-Jaber_al-Sabah" class="mw-redirect" title="Jaber al-Ahmad al-Jaber al-Sabah">Jaber Al-Ahmed</a>, wanted a more spectacular design. This last group, known as <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Towers" title="Kuwait Towers">Kuwait Towers</a>, consists of three towers, two of which also serve as water towers.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> Water from the desalination facility is pumped up to the tower. The thirty-three towers have a standard capacity of 102,000 cubic meters of water. "The Water Towers" (Kuwait Tower and the Kuwait Water Towers) were awarded the <a href="/wiki/Aga_Khan_Award_for_Architecture" title="Aga Khan Award for Architecture">Aga Khan Award for Architecture</a> (1980 Cycle).<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kuwait's fresh water resources are limited to groundwater, desalinated seawater, and treated wastewater effluents.<sup id="cite_ref-scidi_240-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scidi-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> There are three major municipal wastewater treatment plants.<sup id="cite_ref-scidi_240-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scidi-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> Most water demand is currently satisfied through seawater desalination plants.<sup id="cite_ref-scidi_240-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scidi-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fao_241-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fao-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> Sewage disposal is handled by a national sewage network that covers 98% of facilities in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Kuwait" title="Economy of Kuwait">Economy of Kuwait</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kuwait_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Kuwait_Export_Treemap.jpg/350px-Kuwait_Export_Treemap.jpg" decoding="async" width="350" height="273" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Kuwait_Export_Treemap.jpg/525px-Kuwait_Export_Treemap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Kuwait_Export_Treemap.jpg/700px-Kuwait_Export_Treemap.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2670" data-file-height="2086" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kuwait_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A proportional representation of Kuwait's exports</div></div></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r889293853/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:left;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:351px;max-width:351px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:165px;max-width:165px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Alhamra_Tower.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Alhamra_Tower.jpg/163px-Alhamra_Tower.jpg" decoding="async" width="163" height="322" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Alhamra_Tower.jpg/245px-Alhamra_Tower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Alhamra_Tower.jpg/326px-Alhamra_Tower.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1649" data-file-height="3259" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Al_Hamra_Tower" title="Al Hamra Tower">Al Hamra Tower</a> is the tallest sculpted tower in the world.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:182px;max-width:182px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Arrayatower2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Arrayatower2.JPG/180px-Arrayatower2.JPG" decoding="async" width="180" height="323" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Arrayatower2.JPG/270px-Arrayatower2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Arrayatower2.JPG/360px-Arrayatower2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1444" data-file-height="2592" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Arraya_Tower" title="Arraya Tower">Arraya Tower</a></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Kuwait has a <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">petroleum</a>-based economy, petroleum is the main export product. The <a href="/wiki/Kuwaiti_dinar" title="Kuwaiti dinar">Kuwaiti dinar</a> is the highest-valued unit of currency in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-curr_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-curr-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, Kuwait is the seventh richest country in the world <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita#List_of_countries_and_dependencies" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">per capita</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-worldbank_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait is the second richest GCC country per capita (after <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-worldbank_245-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> Petroleum accounts for half of GDP and 90% of government income.<sup id="cite_ref-diver_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diver-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> Non-petroleum industries include financial services.<sup id="cite_ref-diver_248-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diver-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the past five years, there has been a significant rise in <a href="/wiki/Entrepreneurship" title="Entrepreneurship">entrepreneurship</a> and small business start-ups in Kuwait.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Informal_sector" class="mw-redirect" title="Informal sector">informal sector</a> is also on the rise,<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> mainly due to the popularity of Instagram businesses.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kuwait is a major source of foreign economic assistance to other states through the <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Fund_for_Arab_Economic_Development" title="Kuwait Fund for Arab Economic Development">Kuwait Fund for Arab Economic Development</a>, an autonomous state institution created in 1961 on the pattern of international development agencies. In 1974, the fund's lending mandate was expanded to include all <a href="/wiki/Developing_countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Developing countries">developing countries</a> in the world.
</p><p>In 2018 Kuwait enacted certain measures to regulate foreign labor. Citing security concerns, workers from <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a> will be subject to heightened scrutiny when applying for entry visas, and an outright ban was being imposed on the entry of domestic workers from <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau" title="Guinea-Bissau">Guinea-Bissau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> Workers from <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a> are also banned.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Petroleum">Petroleum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Petroleum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_industry_in_Kuwait" title="Petroleum industry in Kuwait">Petroleum industry in Kuwait</a></div>
<p>Despite its relatively small territory, Kuwait has proven crude <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_proven_oil_reserves#Countries" title="List of countries by proven oil reserves">oil reserves</a> of 104&#160;billion barrels, estimated to be 10% of the world's reserves. According to the constitution, all natural resources in the country are state property. Kuwait currently pumps 2.9&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Barrel_per_day" class="mw-redirect" title="Barrel per day">bpd</a> and its full production capacity is a little over 3 million bpd.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Finance">Finance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Finance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Investment_Authority" title="Kuwait Investment Authority">Kuwait Investment Authority</a> (KIA) is Kuwait's <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_wealth_fund" title="Sovereign wealth fund">sovereign wealth fund</a> specializing in foreign investment. The KIA is the world's oldest sovereign wealth fund. Since 1953, the Kuwaiti government has directed investments into Europe, United States and <a href="/wiki/Asia_Pacific" class="mw-redirect" title="Asia Pacific">Asia Pacific</a>. As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the holdings were valued at $592&#160;billion in assets.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> It is the <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_wealth_fund#Largest_sovereign_wealth_funds" title="Sovereign wealth fund">5th largest</a> sovereign wealth fund in the world.
</p><p>Kuwait has a leading position in the financial industry in the GCC; the abyss that separates Kuwait from its Persian Gulf neighbors in terms of tourism, transport, and other measures of diversification is absent in the financial sector.<sup id="cite_ref-wages_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wages-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> The Emir has promoted the idea that Kuwait should focus its energies, in terms of economic development, on the financial industry.<sup id="cite_ref-wages_258-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wages-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The historical preeminence of Kuwait (among the Persian Gulf monarchies) in finance dates back to the founding of the <a href="/wiki/National_Bank_of_Kuwait" title="National Bank of Kuwait">National Bank of Kuwait</a> in 1952.<sup id="cite_ref-wages_258-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wages-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> The bank was the first local publicly traded corporation in the Persian Gulf region.<sup id="cite_ref-wages_258-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wages-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> In the late 1970s and early 1980s, an alternative stock market, trading in shares of Persian Gulf companies, emerged in Kuwait, the <a href="/wiki/Souk_Al-Manakh_stock_market_crash" title="Souk Al-Manakh stock market crash">Souk Al-Manakh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wages_258-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wages-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> At its peak, its market capitalization was the third highest in the world, behind only the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">US</a> and <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, and ahead of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">UK</a> and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wages_258-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wages-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kuwait has a large wealth-management industry that stands out in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-wages_258-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wages-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> Kuwaiti investment companies administer more assets than those of any other GCC country, save the much larger Saudi Arabia.<sup id="cite_ref-wages_258-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wages-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> The Kuwait Financial Centre, in a rough calculation, estimated that Kuwaiti firms accounted for over one-third of the total assets under management in the GCC.<sup id="cite_ref-wages_258-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wages-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> The relative strength of Kuwait in the financial industry extends to its stock market.<sup id="cite_ref-wages_258-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wages-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> For many years, the total valuation of <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_of_Kuwait" title="List of companies of Kuwait">all companies</a> listed on the <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Stock_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Kuwait Stock Exchange">Kuwait Stock Exchange</a> far exceeded the value of those on any other GCC bourse, except Saudi Arabia.<sup id="cite_ref-wages_258-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wages-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, financial and banking companies made up more than half of the market capitalization of the Kuwaiti bourse; among all the Persian Gulf states, the market capitalization of Kuwaiti financial-sector firms was, in total, behind only that of Saudi Arabia.<sup id="cite_ref-wages_258-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wages-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In recent years, Kuwaiti investment companies have invested large percentages of their assets abroad, and their foreign assets have become substantially larger than their domestic assets.<sup id="cite_ref-wages_258-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wages-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_and_research">Health and research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Health and research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Kuwait" title="Health in Kuwait">Health in Kuwait</a></div>
<p>Kuwait has a state-funded <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Kuwait" title="Healthcare in Kuwait">healthcare system</a>, which provides treatment without charge to Kuwaiti nationals. There are outpatient clinics in every residential area in Kuwait. A public insurance scheme exists to provide reduced cost healthcare to expatriates. Private healthcare providers also run medical facilities in the country, available to members of their insurance schemes. There are 29 <a href="/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_Kuwait" title="List of hospitals in Kuwait">public hospitals</a>.  Many new hospitals are under construction.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> The Sheikh Jaber Al-Ahmad Hospital is the largest hospital in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kuwait has a growing scientific research sector. To date, Kuwait has registered 384 <a href="/wiki/Patents" class="mw-redirect" title="Patents">patents</a>, the second highest figure in the Arab world.<sup id="cite_ref-uspto_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uspto-261">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-orient_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-orient-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait produces the largest number of patents per capita in the Arab world and <a href="/wiki/OIC" class="mw-redirect" title="OIC">OIC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mit_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mit-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> The government has implemented various programs to foster innovation resulting in patent rights.<sup id="cite_ref-mit_265-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mit-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gain_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gain-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> Between 2010 and 2016, Kuwait registered the highest growth in patents in the Arab world.<sup id="cite_ref-mit_265-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mit-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-orient_263-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-orient-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gain_269-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gain-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UIS_Literacy_Rate_Kuwait_population_plus15_1975_2015.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/UIS_Literacy_Rate_Kuwait_population_plus15_1975_2015.png/210px-UIS_Literacy_Rate_Kuwait_population_plus15_1975_2015.png" decoding="async" width="210" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/UIS_Literacy_Rate_Kuwait_population_plus15_1975_2015.png/315px-UIS_Literacy_Rate_Kuwait_population_plus15_1975_2015.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5e/UIS_Literacy_Rate_Kuwait_population_plus15_1975_2015.png 2x" data-file-width="399" data-file-height="318" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UIS_Literacy_Rate_Kuwait_population_plus15_1975_2015.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Literacy rate</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Kuwait" title="Education in Kuwait">Education in Kuwait</a></div>
<p>Kuwait has the highest <a href="/wiki/Literacy_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Literacy rate">literacy rate</a> in the Arab world.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup> The general education system consists of four levels:  <a href="/wiki/Kindergarten" title="Kindergarten">kindergarten</a> (lasting for 2 years), <a href="/wiki/Primary_education" title="Primary education">primary</a> (lasting for 5 years), <a href="/wiki/Middle_school" title="Middle school">intermediate</a> (lasting for 4 years) and <a href="/wiki/Secondary_education" title="Secondary education">secondary</a> (lasting for 3 years).<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> Schooling at primary and intermediate level is compulsory for all students aged 6 – 14. All the levels of state education, including higher education, are free.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The public school system is undergoing a revamp due to a project in conjunction with the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-oxfordbusinessgroup_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oxfordbusinessgroup-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, the government launched a pilot project in 48 schools across the state called the National Curriculum Framework.<sup id="cite_ref-oxfordbusinessgroup_273-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oxfordbusinessgroup-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> The curriculum is set to be implemented in the next two or three years.<sup id="cite_ref-oxfordbusinessgroup_273-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oxfordbusinessgroup-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Kuwait" title="Tourism in Kuwait">Tourism in Kuwait</a></div>
<p>Tourism accounts for 1.5 percent of the <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, the tourism industry generated nearly $500&#160;million in revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> The annual "Hala Febrayer" festival attracts many tourists from neighboring GCC countries,<sup id="cite_ref-halafeb_278-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-halafeb-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> and includes a variety of events including music concerts, parades, and carnivals.<sup id="cite_ref-halafeb_278-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-halafeb-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup> The festival is a month-long commemoration of the <a href="/wiki/Liberation_of_Kuwait" class="mw-redirect" title="Liberation of Kuwait">liberation of Kuwait</a>, and runs from 1 to 28 February. <a href="/wiki/Liberation_Day" title="Liberation Day">Liberation Day</a> itself is celebrated on 26 February.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Amiri_Diwan_of_Kuwait" title="Amiri Diwan of Kuwait">Amiri Diwan</a> is currently developing the new <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_National_Cultural_District" title="Kuwait National Cultural District">Kuwait National Cultural District</a> (KNCD), which comprises <a href="/wiki/Sheikh_Abdullah_Al_Salem_Cultural_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheikh Abdullah Al Salem Cultural Centre">Sheikh Abdullah Al Salem Cultural Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheikh_Jaber_Al_Ahmad_Cultural_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheikh Jaber Al Ahmad Cultural Centre">Sheikh Jaber Al Ahmad Cultural Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Shaheed_Park" title="Al Shaheed Park">Al Shaheed Park</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Al_Salam_Palace_(Kuwait)" title="Al Salam Palace (Kuwait)">Al Salam Palace</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kncd_76-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kncd-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kncd2_77-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kncd2-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> With a capital cost of more than US$1&#160;billion, the project is one of the largest cultural investments in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-kncd_76-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kncd-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> In November 2016, the <a href="/wiki/Sheikh_Jaber_Al_Ahmad_Cultural_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheikh Jaber Al Ahmad Cultural Centre">Sheikh Jaber Al Ahmad Cultural Centre</a> opened.<sup id="cite_ref-alb_60-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alb-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> It is the largest cultural centre in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-omnd_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-omnd-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The Kuwait National Cultural District is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Global_Cultural_Districts_Network" title="Global Cultural Districts Network">Global Cultural Districts Network</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gcdn_18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gcdn-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Kuwait" title="Transport in Kuwait">Transport in Kuwait</a></div>
<p>Kuwait has an extensive and modern network of highways. <a href="/wiki/Roads_in_Kuwait" title="Roads in Kuwait">Roadways</a> extended 5,749&#160;km (3,572&#160;mi), of which 4,887&#160;km (3,037&#160;mi) is paved. There are more than two million passenger cars, and 500,000 commercial taxis, buses, and trucks in use. On major highways the maximum speed is 120&#160;km/h (75&#160;mph). Since there is no railway system in the country, most people travel by automobiles.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kuwait_highway.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Kuwait_highway.jpg/220px-Kuwait_highway.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Kuwait_highway.jpg/330px-Kuwait_highway.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Kuwait_highway.jpg/440px-Kuwait_highway.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3100" data-file-height="2325" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kuwait_highway.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A highway in Kuwait City</div></div></div>
<p>The country's public transportation network consists almost entirely of bus routes. The state owned Kuwait Public Transportation Company was established in 1962. It runs local bus routes across Kuwait as well as longer distance services to other <a href="/wiki/Arab_states_of_the_Persian_Gulf" title="Arab states of the Persian Gulf">Gulf states</a>. The main private bus company is CityBus, which operates about 20 routes across the country. Another private bus company, Kuwait Gulf Link Public Transport Services, was started in 2006. It runs local bus routes across Kuwait and longer distance services to neighbouring Arab countries.
</p><p>There are two airports in Kuwait. <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_International_Airport" title="Kuwait International Airport">Kuwait International Airport</a> serves as the principal hub for international air travel. State-owned <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Airways" title="Kuwait Airways">Kuwait Airways</a> is the largest airline in the country. A portion of the airport complex is designated as Al Mubarak Air Base, which contains the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Air_Force" title="Kuwait Air Force">Kuwait Air Force</a>, as well as the Kuwait Air Force Museum. In 2004, the first private airline of Kuwait, <a href="/wiki/Jazeera_Airways" title="Jazeera Airways">Jazeera Airways</a>, was launched. In 2005, the second private airline, <a href="/wiki/Wataniya_Airways" title="Wataniya Airways">Wataniya Airways</a> was founded.
</p><p>Kuwait has one of the largest shipping industries in the region. The Kuwait Ports Public Authority manages and operates ports across Kuwait. The country's principal commercial seaports are <a href="/wiki/Shuwaikh" class="mw-redirect" title="Shuwaikh">Shuwaikh</a> and Shuaiba, which handled combined cargo of 753,334 TEU in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup> Mina Al-Ahmadi, the largest port in the country, handles most of Kuwait's oil exports.<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup> Construction of another major port located in <a href="/wiki/Bubiyan" class="mw-redirect" title="Bubiyan">Bubiyan</a> island started in 2007. The port is expected to handle 1.3&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Twenty-foot_equivalent_unit" title="Twenty-foot equivalent unit">TEU</a> when operations start.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Kuwait" title="Demographics of Kuwait">Demographics of Kuwait</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kuwaityouth5020.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Kuwaityouth5020.jpg/220px-Kuwaityouth5020.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Kuwaityouth5020.jpg/330px-Kuwaityouth5020.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Kuwaityouth5020.jpg/440px-Kuwaityouth5020.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4256" data-file-height="2832" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kuwaityouth5020.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kuwaiti youth celebrating Kuwait's independence and liberation, 2011</div></div></div>
<p>Kuwait's 2018 population was 4.6&#160;million people, of which 1.4&#160;million were Kuwaitis, 1.2&#160;million are other Arabs, 1.8&#160;million Asian expatriates,<sup id="cite_ref-PACI_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PACI-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> and 47,227 Africans.<sup id="cite_ref-gulfnews.com_284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gulfnews.com-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Expatriates_in_Kuwait" title="Expatriates in Kuwait">Expatriates in Kuwait</a> account for around 70% of Kuwait's total population. In end of December 2018, 57.65% of Kuwait's total population are <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arabs</a> (including Arab expats).<sup id="cite_ref-PACI_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PACI-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Indian_people" title="Indian people">Indians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Egyptians" title="Egyptians">Egyptians</a> are the largest expat communities respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Kuwait" title="Religion in Kuwait">Religion in Kuwait</a></div>
<p>Most Kuwaiti citizens are Muslim; it is estimated that 60%–65% are Sunni and 35%–40% are Shias.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ssi_288-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ssi-288">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup> Most <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam_in_Kuwait" title="Shia Islam in Kuwait">Shia Kuwaiti citizens</a> are of <a href="/wiki/%27Ajam_of_Kuwait" title="&#39;Ajam of Kuwait">Persian ancestry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup> The country includes a <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Kuwait#Kuwaiti_Christians" title="Christianity in Kuwait">native Christian</a> community, estimated to be composed of between 259 and 400 Christian Kuwaiti citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-ref_296-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ref-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait is the only <a href="/wiki/Cooperation_Council_for_the_Arab_States_of_the_Gulf" class="mw-redirect" title="Cooperation Council for the Arab States of the Gulf">GCC country</a> besides Bahrain to have a local Christian population who hold citizenship. There is also a small number of <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahá&#39;í">Bahá'í</a> Kuwaiti citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-irfr2007_297-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-irfr2007-297">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup> Kuwait also has a large community of expatriate <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hindus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhists</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-irfr2007_297-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-irfr2007-297">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>Religion by Nationality in Kuwait (2018)<sup id="cite_ref-PACI_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PACI-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></b>
</p>

<p>Note:<br />
– Christians from Asia in Kuwait mostly come from the Philippines, South Korea, and some from Indonesia, Malaysia, India and other countries.<br />
– Muslims from Asia in Kuwait mostly come from Indonesia, Malaysia, Pakistan, Kazakhstan, Kyrgyzstan and other countries.<br />
– Hindus from Asia in Kuwait mostly come from India, and Sri Lanka.<br />
– Buddhists from Asia in Kuwait mostly come from China, Thailand and Vietnam.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kuwait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Kuwaiti_Arabic" title="Kuwaiti Arabic">Kuwaiti Arabic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kuwaiti_Persian" title="Kuwaiti Persian">Kuwaiti Persian</a></div>
<p>Kuwait's official language is <a href="/wiki/Modern_Standard_Arabic" title="Modern Standard Arabic">Modern Standard Arabic</a>, but its everyday usage is limited to journalism and education. <a href="/wiki/Kuwaiti_Arabic" title="Kuwaiti Arabic">Kuwaiti Arabic</a> is the variant of Arabic used in everyday life.<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> is widely understood and often used as a business language. Beside English, <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> is taught as a third language for the students of the <a href="/wiki/Humanities" title="Humanities">humanities</a> at schools, but for two years only. Kuwaiti Arabic is a variant of <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Arabic" title="Gulf Arabic">Gulf Arabic</a>, sharing similarities with the dialects of neighboring coastal areas in Eastern Arabia.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup> Due to immigration during its early history as well as trade, Kuwaiti Arabic borrowed a lot of words from <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_India" title="Languages of India">Indian languages</a>, <a href="/wiki/Balochi_language" title="Balochi language">Balochi language</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Due to historical immigration, <a href="/wiki/Kuwaiti_Persian" title="Kuwaiti Persian">Kuwaiti Persian</a> is used among <a href="/wiki/%27Ajam_of_Kuwait" title="&#39;Ajam of Kuwait">Ajam Kuwaitis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Iranian_languages" title="Iranian languages">Iranian</a> sub-dialects of <a href="/wiki/Larestani" class="mw-redirect" title="Larestani">Larestani</a>, Khonji, Bastaki and Gerashi also influenced the vocabulary of Kuwaiti Arabic.<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-thae-108"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-thae_108-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-thae_108-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.y-oman.com/2013/07/shooting-the-past/">"Shooting the Past"</a>. <i>y-oman.com</i>. 11 July 2013. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20160505143238/https://www.y-oman.com/2013/07/shooting-the-past/">Archived</a> from the original on 5 May 2016. <q>Most Omanis who get to study drama abroad tend to go to Kuwait or Egypt. In the Persian Gulf, Kuwait has long been a pioneer in theatre, film and television since the establishment of its Higher Institute of Dramatic Arts (HIDA) in 1973. By contrast, there is no drama college or film school in Oman, although there is a drama course at Sultan Qaboos University.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=y-oman.com&amp;rft.atitle=Shooting+the+Past&amp;rft.date=2013-07-11&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.y-oman.com%2F2013%2F07%2Fshooting-the-past%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AKuwait" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
